<div id="review_2676849743" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2676849743" />
    <a title="Faith Wisniewski" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92272220-faith-wisniewski"><img alt="Faith Wisniewski" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2676849743?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith Wisniewski" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith Wisniewski" href="/user/show/92272220-faith-wisniewski">Faith Wisniewski</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2676849743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14615721736663330965">R<br/>Name: Faith Wisniewski<br/><br/>Book title: Second Helpings<br/><br/>Personal Response:<br/>Personally, I really enjoyed reading this book. I normally do not enjoy reading, but I couldn't put this book down. <i> Second Helpings </i> is the second book in the series. I did not read the first one and I understood what was going on in this book, so you do not need to read the series in order. Megan McCafferty is a very good author. Her writings are very descriptive! I would definitely read <i> Second Helpings</i> again.<br/><br/>Book Summary:<br/><i>Sec</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14615721736663330965" style="display:none">R<br />Name: Faith Wisniewski<br /><br />Book title: Second Helpings<br /><br />Personal Response:<br />Personally, I really enjoyed reading this book. I normally do not enjoy reading, but I couldn't put this book down. <i> Second Helpings </i> is the second book in the series. I did not read the first one and I understood what was going on in this book, so you do not need to read the series in order. Megan McCafferty is a very good author. Her writings are very descriptive! I would definitely read <i> Second Helpings</i> again.<br /><br />Book Summary:<br /><i>Second Helpings</i> starts by introducing Jessica Darling, the main character as a normal teenage girl. She keeps a journal and the book is made up of her journal entries. Jessica goes to a summer camp where she explores writing. This happens on accident though because Jessica only signed up for the camp so that she would not have to go to cross country camp. A few weeks into the camp Jessica accidentally leaves her personal journal for her instructor to read instead of her writing journal. Which could end up super bad because she wrote embarrassing things about her teacher.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Jessica's teacher approached her the next day to tell her what a great writer is and how she should use that kind of emotion in all of her work.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> A few weeks after the incident Jessica's class visits a famous poetry place in New York. Instead of going to read her poetry Jessica bumps into an old friend and he gives her a tour of Columbia's campus. Jessica falls in love with the college immediately and decides that she wants to attend school there. Jessica is top of her class with one other kid. Len and Jessica are the “class brainiacs”, Len has a crush on Jessica but she's too busy obsessing over his best friend to notice. Even though she won't admit it Jessica has a huge crush on Marcus. Marcus is a bad influence though. In <i>Sloppy Firsts</i> Marcus play mind games with Jessica and made a game out of trying to hook up with her, so now she doesn't trust him. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Now Marcus actually likes Jessica  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Jessica and Len end up dating for three months, before Len breaks things off with Jessica because they share different viewpoints on a topic that is very important to Len. In the end, everyone ends up happy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Jessica and Marcus end up together and Jessica gets accepted into Columbia. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Recommendation: <br />I would recommend this book to young adults, and possibly more mature teenagers. <i> Second Helpings </i> contains a lot of adult jokes but is still very funny<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14615721736663330965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8893314561652204013">This book continued to be an overall fun, enjoyable and distracting experience for me.<br/><br/>That being said this series contains so many problematic... Words and elements it is kinda amazing the book is only what 16 years old? Haha as old as Jessica Darling around the beginning of the series.<br/><br/>As I have read others say, it's ... Achievable to let Jessica Notso Darling's anti-pc language and agenda slide given she is a dumb teenager. I too was once a dumb teenager and had my own slut shaming tendencies, </span>
  <span id="freeText8893314561652204013" style="display:none">This book continued to be an overall fun, enjoyable and distracting experience for me.<br /><br />That being said this series contains so many problematic... Words and elements it is kinda amazing the book is only what 16 years old? Haha as old as Jessica Darling around the beginning of the series.<br /><br />As I have read others say, it's ... Achievable to let Jessica Notso Darling's anti-pc language and agenda slide given she is a dumb teenager. I too was once a dumb teenager and had my own slut shaming tendencies, implicit bias and racism and shit to fight against that I am still fighting against. But according to reviews of the later books even as Jessica ages, apparently she doesn't grow up in these respects.<br /><br />Personally, I think the second book wraps things up well enough. So this is likely where I will part with McCafferty's series. <br /><br />That is more a personal reminder than anything else. Gotta stay strong and read something different from my long long to read list, which likely contains so titles that I will enjoy that won't simultaneously make me want to sanitize my mind.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DujSQDcDW7ekZ3BALXXtZZr5ev5r+Hzov7tQFE+GOLZqWE2uQMi8LIYEamjqoeEucUWXYZs39rn9CZcdkTiyhA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SX2GHPyst66KnLH6Apqxl1YsrzrmQBMTZD63o8qviIktzRnyi2dQNaj/q9LFTr3cvZBCpRaPmUImjHCqFBECuw==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14958671466560734013">Megan McCafferty writes fiction for tweens, teens and teens-at-heart of all ages. The author of eleven novels, she’s best known for SLOPPY FIRSTS and four more sequels in the New York Times bestselling Jessica Darling series.   <span id="freeText14958671466560734013" style="display:none">Megan McCafferty writes fiction for tweens, teens and teens-at-heart of all ages.
